Groundwater Pollution: United Nations Environment Program
(Question No. 3007)
Mr Jacobi asked the Minister representing the Minister for National Development and Energy, upon notice, on 9 September 1981:
(1) Can the Minister say whether the pollution threat to Earth's water is one of the emerging dangers featured in the 1981 State of the World Environment Report from the United Nations Environment Program in Nairobi.
(2) If so, has the UN Environment Program identified the need to protect our supplies of usable groundwater as one of three topics which are especially timely.
(3) Does the Minister support this element of the UN program; if so, what action will be taken to protect groundwaters in Australia.
Mr Anthony-The Minister for National Development and Energy has provided the following answer to the honourable member's question:
(I) Yes.
(2) Yes.
(3) Yes. Support for this element of the report is consistent with the Government's water policy statement as set out in the House of Representatives Hansard, pages 1211-1213, 28 March 1979. The Government is providing funds for research and assessment activities relating to Australia's groundwater resources and the report will be referred to the Groundwater Committee of the Australian Water Resources Council for its consideration.

Groundwater Pollution Conference
(Question No. 3062)
Mr Jacobi asked the Minister representing the Minister for National Development and Energy, upon notice, on 9 September 1981:
(1) Has the Minister's attention been drawn to the recently published proceedings of the Groundwater Pollution Conference, which was supported by the Australian Water Resources Council.

(2) Has Australia developed criteria for groundwater quality in the 2t years since the conference was held as recommended by the conference participants; if not, why not.
(3) Has intergovernmental support been provided for research into (a) the land treatment and groundwater treatment of waste-water and (b) microbiological and radio-active pollution.
(4) Has intergovernmental co-operation been reached to develop guidelines for the monitoring and management of the quality of groundwater, as recommended by conference participants; if so, what is the extent and nature of this support; if not, why not.
(5) What action has been taken to promote each of the specific research needs, and to promote the direction of future research into groundwater pollution in Australia as envisaged by conference participants, namely (a) the increased study of the fundamentals of solute movement in the unsaturated zone, in heterogeneous rocks and in fractured rocks, (b )the determination of whether solute dispersion in aquifers is velocity dependent, (c) the development of equipment and guidelines for obtaining representative samples from bores, (d) the urgent need to develop practical techniques for determining trace viruses in water, (e) the determination of the life cycle of pathogens and the persistence of carcinogenic substances in groundwater and (f) the identification of groundwater systems likely to be affected by future development and evaluation of the efficiency of local industry's effiuent disposal techniques.
(6) Which bodies or authorities have undertaken this work and how has this research been co-ordinated.
(7) Did the summary of the conference state that management (of groundwater) was seen to be a responsibility of government and specify that this should be integrated with national development planning; if so, does he support this statement and what action has been taken, or will be taken, to give effect to the recommendation.
(8) If he does not support the recommendation referred to in part (7), what is the reason.
Mr Anthony-The Minister for National Development and Energy has provided the following answer to the honourable member's question:
(1) Yes.
(2) The Australian Water Resources Council (AWRC) and the National Health and Medical Research Council (NHMRC), in collaboration, have recommended guidelines on desirable quality for drinking water in Australia. These guidelines apply equally to surface and underground water.
(3) to (8) Prior to, and since the Groundwater Pollution Conference, the Commonwealth has provided funds under the research program of the Australian Water Resources Council for many projects in the research areas identified by the honourable member. Summaries of these projects are included in the Inventory of Water Resources Research in Australia which has been published by the Department of National Development and Energy or its predecessors in eight editions since 1965. Information on groundwater-related research topics can be readily identified, including the source of funds. The collaborative Commonwealth-States water resources assessment program continues to provide valuable information on the quantity and quality of Australia's ground water resources, and the AWRC Groundwater Committee provides a valuable forum for the consideration at the national level of groundwater issues.
In relation to research issues emanating from the Groundwater Pollution Conference, they will be considered by the Groundwater Committee of the Australian Water Resources Council at its next meeting as a basis for advice to the Council

1656 REPRESENTATIVES 22 September 1981

Answers to Questions

on desirable action within the Council's collaborative machinery.
In addition, the AWRC is sponsoring a seminar on the assessment and management of groundwater in fractured rocks, to be held in Canberra between 31 August and 3 September 1982, and an international conference on groundwater for late 1983. Planning for this conference is at an early stage, but it is likely to deal with assessment, pollution and development aspects of groundwater.
Victorian College of Pharmacy
Mr MacKellar-On 15 September 1981 (Hansard page 1286), the honourable member for Melbourne (Mr Innes) asked me a question without notice concerning the funding of the Victorian College of Pharmacy.

The Minister for Educatiop has provided the following answer to the honourable member's question:
Funding for the Victorian College of Pharmacy falls within the Commonwealth's grants program for advanced education. The Government has indicated the total level or recurrent funds to be provided for higher education over the 1982-84 triennium and the Commonwealth Tertiary Education Commission; and its constituent Councils, have been in consultation with State and institutional authorities on the detailed distribution of available funds among institutions. J expect to be in a position to table the Commission's report shortly. The report will include recommendations on the level of recurrent grants to be provided to the Victorian College of Pharmacy over the fourthcoming triennium.
